## Analysis

The GT numerical expression is:
$$f(x,v) = -0.661172493025524\,v - 1.16984597672115\,x^3 - 0.330586246512762\,\log(|v| + 1)$$

This consists of three terms:
1. A term linear in $v$
2. A term proportional to $x^3$
3. A $\log(|v| + 1)$ term

Now I need to find a candidate that can reproduce this. The key challenge is the $\log(|v| + 1)$ term. Let me examine candidates with logarithmic terms involving $v$.

Many candidates have $\log(c \cdot v^2 + 1)$ terms. Note that $\log(|v|+1) \neq \log(v^2+1)$ in general, so these won't match exactly.

Some candidates have $\log(c_7 \exp(c_8 v) + 1)$ terms (candidates 3, 7, 8, 19, 29, 30, 36, 46).

**Candidate 30**: $c_0 x^3 + c_1 x^2 + c_2 x + c_3 + c_4 \log(c_5 \exp(c_6 v) + 1)$

Setting $c_1 = 0$, $c_2 = 0$, $c_3 = 0$, $c_0 = -1.16984597672115$.

We need $c_4 \log(c_5 \exp(c_6 v) + 1)$ to equal $-0.661172493025524\,v - 0.330586246512762\,\log(|v| + 1)$.

This is a single log term versus two different functional forms, so this won't work for all $v$.

**Candidate 42**: $c_0 x^3 + c_1 x^2 + c_2 x + c_3 + c_4 v \exp(c_5 x) + c_6 \log(c_7 v^2 + 1) + c_8 v x^2 + c_9 v$

Setting $c_1=0, c_2=0, c_3=0, c_8=0$ (to kill $x^2$, $x$, constant, $vx^2$ terms), and $c_5=0$ so $c_4 v \exp(0) = c_4 v$.

Then: $c_0 x^3 + (c_4 + c_9)v + c_6 \log(c_7 v^2 + 1)$

We need this to equal $-1.16985\,x^3 - 0.66117\,v - 0.33059\,\log(|v|+1)$.

The issue is $\log(c_7 v^2 + 1)$ vs $\log(|v|+1)$. These are fundamentally different functions — $\log(v^2+1)$ is not proportional to $\log(|v|+1)$ for all $v$.

However, let me reconsider candidates with $v\cdot|v|$ terms (which equals $v\cdot\text{sgn}(v)\cdot|v| = |v|\cdot v$... no, $v|v| = \text{sgn}(v) v^2$).

**Candidate 36**: $c_0 x^3 + c_1 x^2 + c_2 x + c_3 + c_4 v x^2 + c_5 \log(c_6 \exp(c_7 v) + 1)$

Set $c_1=c_2=c_3=0$, $c_4=0$. Then: $c_0 x^3 + c_5 \log(c_6 \exp(c_7 v)+1)$.

For $v > 0$: if $c_7 < 0$ and $c_6 = 1$: $\log(\exp(c_7 v)+1) \approx c_7 v$ for large negative $c_7 v$... This can approximate but not exactly equal $-0.66117v - 0.33059\log(|v|+1)$ for all $v$.

After careful analysis, **Candidate 42** is the closest structural match. While $\log(c_7 v^2 + 1)$ isn't identical to $\log(|v|+1)$, note that if we set $c_7 = 0$ and use the $c_4 v \exp(c_5 x)$ and $c_9 v$ terms... we still can't get the log term.

GT Equivalence Verification (PO6)

GT: -beta*log(Abs(v) + c0) - c1*beta*v - omega0**c2*x**c3
Candidates evaluated: 50
Matched candidate IDs: []

I need to determine which candidates can be made equivalent to the GT:

**GT:** `-0.661172493025524*v - 1.16984597672115*x**3 - 0.330586246512762*log(Abs(v) + 1)`

The GT has three terms:
1. A term linear in `v`
2. A term `x**3`
3. A term `log(|v| + 1)`

Key observation: `log(|v| + 1)` is NOT the same as `log(v² + 1)` or `log(exp(v) + 1)`. I need to check carefully.

Note: `log(|v| + 1)` vs `log(c*v² + 1)`: These are fundamentally different functions. `log(|v|+1)` has a cusp at v=0 and grows as log(|v|), while `log(v²+1)` is smooth and grows as `2*log(|v|)`. They are NOT equivalent.

`log(c*exp(c*v) + 1)`: This is a softplus-type function. For large positive v, it's approximately linear; for large negative v, it approaches 0. Meanwhile `log(|v|+1)` grows logarithmically in both directions. NOT equivalent.

However, let me reconsider: can `log(|v|+1)` be decomposed? No, it's a specific basis function.

Let me check which candidates contain `log(Abs(v) + c)` or equivalent:

Looking through all candidates:
- Candidates with `log(c*v**2 + 1)`: 1, 2, 4, 9, 25, 31, 34, 40, 42, 48, 50 — NOT equivalent to `log(|v|+1)`
- Candidates with `log(c*exp(c*v) + 1)`: 3, 7, 8, 19, 29, 30, 36, 46 — NOT equivalent
- Candidates with `log(c*x**2 + c*v**2 + 1)`: 11, 17, 47 — NOT equivalent
- Candidates with `log(c*Abs(v) + 1)`: 6, 15, 16 — these have `x**2*log(c*Abs(v)+1)`, which couples x² with the log term
- Candidates with `v*Abs(v)`: various — this equals `v|v|`, sign(v)*v², NOT equivalent to `log(|v|+1)`

For candidates 6, 15, 16: They have `c4*x**2*log(c5*Abs(v) + 1)`. To get `log(|v|+1)` without the x² factor, I'd need to set c4=0, but then the log term vanishes entirely. These candidates don't have a standalone `log(|v|+1)` term.

None of the candidates contain a standalone `log(Abs(v) + c)` term. The GT requires this specific basis function, and by the principle of linear independence of basis functions, no combination of the available terms (polynomials, exponentials, `v*|v|`, `log(v²+1)`, `log(exp(v)+1)`, etc.) can reproduce `log(|v|+1)`.

Let me verify once more: Is there any way `log(v²+1)` could equal `log(|v|+1)` up to constants? No: `log(v²+1) = log((|v|-1)² + 2|v|)` — these are fundamentally different functions.

Therefore, **none** of the candidates match.
